  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_71ebcd35-86a0-48f0-928a-b043c8fc3891'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

  <span id="freeText15823911203803627319" style="display:none"><b>Once a century, one person is chosen for greatness.</b><br />Elisa is the chosen one. <br /><br />But she is also the younger of two princesses, the one who has never done anything remarkable. She can't see how she ever will. <br /><br />Now, on her sixteenth birthday, she has become the secret wife of a handsome and worldly king—a king whose country is in turmoil. A king who needs the chosen one, not a failure of a princess.<br /><br />And he's not the only one who seeks her. Savage enemies seething with dark magic are hunting her. A daring, determined revolutionary thinks she could be his people's savior. And he looks at her in a way that no man has ever looked at her before. Soon it is not just her life, but her very heart that is at stake.<br /><br />Elisa could be everything to those who need her most. If the prophecy is fulfilled. If she finds the power deep within herself. If she doesn’t die young.<br /><br />Most of the chosen do.</span>

      $('edition_13624038').observe('prototip:shown', function() {
        if (this.up('#box')) {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_13624038').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_13624038').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_13624038').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();

<div id="review_346181967" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/346181967" />
    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2016128-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572638169p2/2016128.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/346181967?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/2016128-shannon">Shannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11183955-the-girl-of-fire-and-thorns">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Shannon by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3701038-elena">Elena</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=terrible-writing">terrible-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=color-brown">color-brown</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=color-blue">color-blue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=waste-of-time">waste-of-time</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer346181967" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer146806133855634034">If you caught even just a couple of my updates I think it would've been plainly obvious that I didn't enjoy this book. It's disappointing, really, because I think Carson was attempting to create a heroine that many girls could relate to. Elisa is overweight, unsure of herself, overshadowed by her prettier and skinnier sister, and chosen for something she's not sure she's worthy of. It sounds like the beginning of a compelling story, but ultimately <b>Elisa only proves her worthiness by changing eve</b></span>
  <span id="freeText146806133855634034" style="display:none">If you caught even just a couple of my updates I think it would've been plainly obvious that I didn't enjoy this book. It's disappointing, really, because I think Carson was attempting to create a heroine that many girls could relate to. Elisa is overweight, unsure of herself, overshadowed by her prettier and skinnier sister, and chosen for something she's not sure she's worthy of. It sounds like the beginning of a compelling story, but ultimately <b>Elisa only proves her worthiness by changing everything about herself.</b> And walking. A lot.<br /><br /><b>Elisa is fat and likes to eat.</b> You will hear about the food she eats and the sweets she craves so often that you'll start to wonder if you're reading a thinly veiled advertisement instead, or if this book was sponsored by the coconut or lamb industry. This girl eats so many scones. And when she's not eating, she's thinking about her next meal or about what she had the day before. Even after Elisa loses some weight and doesn't need to shove food down her gullet 24/7 to stave off headaches and fatigue, the story still revolves around her meals. I didn't need to know what she was eating every single day, or how it was prepared or who prepared it or how it tasted ... really. Cut out the food descriptions and this book would've been half as long. I get it, Elisa likes food and has a love/hate relationship with it. <b>Am I reading a fantasy story or the food diary of a girl with an eating disorder?</b><br /><br />After food, <b>a large amount of the story is spent on Elisa walking from point A to point B.</b> Sometimes with other people, sometimes against her will, sometimes alone. So then all of that walking means fat Elisa becomes skinny Elisa and all of her problems start melting away along with the pounds; people think she can win their war, boys fall in love with her, girls want to be her best friend. And the Godstone in her belly (that she can now see without parting her breasts and moving her stomach fat out of the way - wut) starts to react to danger, helping her elude her enemies. Because God rewards you when you're not fat!<br /><br /><b>There are also plot holes</b> (and really, not a whole lot of <i>plot</i> to begin with) and at one point a character remarks that they have no idea why the enemy is attacking. <b>The magic is incredibly underdeveloped and mostly relies on praying and hoping something will happen.</b> Generals, guards, and the King all look to Elisa for war counsel when all she had ever done was read this world's version of <i>The Art of War</i>. The first person <i>I'd</i> look to for advice during war would definitely be a 16-year-old girl.<br /><br /><b>Elisa's hair-brained schemes work because the author wants them to.</b> Everything is conveniently tied up with a neat little bow and there's not a single surprise. In the end, I was so unattached to any of the characters that I barely even blinked when someone died. <br /><br />Elisa has a magic stone in her belly button, she's good at memorizing stuff, has blind faith in God, and knows the best pastry recipes. Those are her special powers. <b>Elisa is a boring character surrounded by other boring characters living out a boring story with food being a much more developed entity than any of the people or the plot.</b> I will probably not continue with this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="146806133855634034" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2395175784" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2395175784" />
    <a title="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake"><img alt="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605987751p2/11626803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2395175784?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" href="/user/show/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake">Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/13624038-the-girl-of-fire-and-thorns">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake?shelf=0-in-my-library-read">0-in-my-library-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2395175784" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer527231838124119138"><b>Dude. You guys. Best YA high fantasy I’ve read in, well, a LONG time.</b><br/> <br/>And one of the few 5 star ratings my stingy ass has handed out so far this year.<br/><br/>I did the old, “I’ll just read a couple of chapters before bed” nonsense and....yeah. Read it in one sitting. <br/><br/>The writing was engrossing, the plot moved along at a decent pace, and the characters were all layered and grew/developed throughout the story. <br/><br/>I also loved that the main character - although still a "chosen one" trope character - was not a</span>
  <span id="freeText527231838124119138" style="display:none"><b>Dude. You guys. Best YA high fantasy I’ve read in, well, a LONG time.</b><br /> <br />And one of the few 5 star ratings my stingy ass has handed out so far this year.<br /><br />I did the old, “I’ll just read a couple of chapters before bed” nonsense and....yeah. Read it in one sitting. <br /><br />The writing was engrossing, the plot moved along at a decent pace, and the characters were all layered and grew/developed throughout the story. <br /><br />I also loved that the main character - although still a "chosen one" trope character - was not a cliched, archetype. <br /><br />She was described as fairly insecure.<br />Not all that pretty.<br />And, as the book explicitly states - I'm not just being a bitch here (for once) - FAT. <br /><br />Which was cool to see. <br /><br />It's nice to have more varied and realistic characters playing the "hero" character these days, a character that used to be traditionally reserved solely for the perfect, hot (or hot but doesn't <i>realize</i> they are hot *eye roll*) character...especially as applied to female protagonists. <br /><br />That said...I must say this. <br /><br />I got a little nervous that I wasn't going to be able to finish this book. <br /><br />And here's why.<br /><br />I've discussed this before in another review somewhere - and I'm just too lazy to rehash it right now - but I've struggled with an eating disorder since my early teens. I have had it basically under control (or as much as you can "control" such things) since my mid-late 20's, but every now and then, something can start to trigger old habits. <br /><br />And boy did this book start triggering me like none other. <br /><br />As I said, the main character is fat. And who cares. Not me. <br /><br />However, there is almost <i>constant</i> mention of her eating and thinking about eating. <br />And, not just eating, but unhealthily-bingeing-and-eating-my-feelings-style eating. <br /><br />Now, for people who don't have eating disorders or know someone with one, it can be very difficult to understand. It seems silly and vain and should be solved with a simple, "Oh, just eat something," right?<br /><br />Not so much.<br /><br />Once you get in that mental space, it's very difficult to get out. Like, we are talking simple shit having the potential to trigger months/years of backsliding for me, as lame as that sounds. <br /><br />So lame.<br />So silly. <br />SO legit. <br /><br />But anyway. I don't want to beat a dead horse here or bore you with bullshit. <br /><br />Long story, short: The constant talk of eating here started to make me a little nervous and I could feel once dead mental baggage start to rear up a bit; but thankfully, the story eventually moved forward from the constant mention of food, etc. <br /><br />The Author Notes at the end - which I really enjoyed reading also - delved into why exactly Carson made her MC the way she did (as applied to weight and appearance) and I really appreciated her commentary. <br /><br />But anyway, enough bullshit TMI no one cares about. <br /><br />This is a great YA fantasy with a really great female MC and I would recommend it highly if you are interested in this genre.</span>
  <a data-text-id="527231838124119138" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1342780455" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer542973454474675731"><b>I feel torn about <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10429092.The_Girl_of_Fire_and_Thorns__Fire_and_Thorns___1_' title='The Girl of Fire and Thorns (Fire and Thorns, #1) by Rae Carson' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Girl of Fire and Thorns</a>.</b><br/><br/>On the one hand, there's not much room to accuse this book of being slow - the action is constant, zipping along from a bloody battle, to a lusty encounter (PG-13, of course), to another dramatic reveal, to a kidnapping. Elisa's life spins off in a crazy new direction that starts with her marriage to a King of a nearby country in chapter one, and the pacing never slows down after that.<br/><br/>Elisa is a 16-year-old princess and was born the bearer of a Godst</span>
  <span id="freeText542973454474675731" style="display:none"><b>I feel torn about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10429092.The_Girl_of_Fire_and_Thorns__Fire_and_Thorns___1_" title="The Girl of Fire and Thorns (Fire and Thorns, #1) by Rae Carson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl of Fire and Thorns</a>.</b><br /><br />On the one hand, there's not much room to accuse this book of being slow - the action is constant, zipping along from a bloody battle, to a lusty encounter (PG-13, of course), to another dramatic reveal, to a kidnapping. Elisa's life spins off in a crazy new direction that starts with her marriage to a King of a nearby country in chapter one, and the pacing never slows down after that.<br /><br />Elisa is a 16-year-old princess and was born the bearer of a Godstone (a literal gift from God that rests in her navel). Because of this, Elisa must follow in the footsteps of other Godstone-bearers and perform a special service to God. Nobody knows what it will be. In fact, Elisa knows very little about her destiny and the lives of those who came before her. Many secrets will be revealed as the story moves along.<br /><br />To be honest, though, the action only barely masks an incredibly messy and ill-conceived plot. Despite being a very different kind of story, I would compare it to books like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13335037.Divergent__Divergent___1_" title="Divergent (Divergent, #1) by Veronica Roth" rel="nofollow noopener">Divergent</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6186357.The_Maze_Runner__Maze_Runner___1_" title="The Maze Runner (Maze Runner, #1) by James Dashner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Maze Runner</a>, in that it has lots of flashy action and fast pacing, but underneath there lurks mediocre writing, all tell and no show, and flat characters separated into the "beautiful" and the unattractive/fat.<br /><br /><b>Elisa is characterized by her fatness</b>. Am I glad that authors are creating heroines that are not all skinny, beautiful, white girls? Of course I am. But I feel like being fat and unattractive is the defining characteristic of Elisa. It might make her different, but alone it's not enough to make her interesting. <br /><br />I recently read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24202275.Sugar" title="Sugar by Deirdre Riordan Hall" rel="nofollow noopener">Sugar</a> - another book about an overweight girl - and the protagonist's characterization is fascinating. I understood her complex relationship with food, her need to constantly eat, and her self-loathing when she did. Elisa is so one-dimensional in comparison.<br /><br />Also, I'm surprised many reviewers haven't pointed out how... <i>religious</i> this is. I don't know if Religious Fantasy is a sub-genre but I find myself thinking it should be to accommodate Carson's book. Religion and praying play huge roles in this story. If you took the magical elements out, I could almost see this as your standard Christian novel.<br /><br />I recommend this with some hesitation, and mainly to those who don't mind an action-packed plot with little substance behind it.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="542973454474675731" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_170223838" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/170223838" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/170223838?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of &quot;Divergent,&quot; &quot;Matched,&quot; &quot;Delirium&quot;</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Tatiana by: </span>
      Paolo Bacigalupi's blurb
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=morris">morris</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=why-the-hype">why-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer170223838" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4817623502722082745">2.5 stars<br/><br/>My ARC has the old version of the cover and it is super pretty, the blue tones of it are gorgeous:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379771198i/296027._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I am glad the publishers changed it though. At the very least this book will be spared accusations of whitewashing and weightwashing. The heroine of this novel - Princess Elisa of Orovalle - describes herself as "dark," "brown" and also as "a big, bloated sausage" and "pig." Clearly, the cover doesn't <i>quite</i> match these adjectives.<br/><br/>Now onto the novel itself. 16-year old princess Elisa has a g</span>
  <span id="freeText4817623502722082745" style="display:none">2.5 stars<br><br>My ARC has the old version of the cover and it is super pretty, the blue tones of it are gorgeous:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379771198i/296027._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I am glad the publishers changed it though. At the very least this book will be spared accusations of whitewashing and weightwashing. The heroine of this novel - Princess Elisa of Orovalle - describes herself as "dark," "brown" and also as "a big, bloated sausage" and "pig." Clearly, the cover doesn't <i>quite</i> match these adjectives.<br><br>Now onto the novel itself. 16-year old princess Elisa has a gift from God - a magical stone (Godstone) that she bears in her navel. As a Godstone-bearer, Elisa is fated to do a special Service for God, an act of heroism. What it is, nobody knows, especially not Elisa, who considers herself a fat, useless child. The Princess gets a glimpse of her purpose when she first becomes a wife of the King of a neighboring country and later is kidnapped by local rebels.<br><br>The strongest points of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8419564.The_Girl_of_Fire_and_Thorns__Fire_and_Thorns___1_" title="The Girl of Fire and Thorns (Fire and Thorns, #1) by Rae Carson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl of Fire and Thorns</a> are its plotting and pacing. The plot is engaging with some intriguing and trekking moving things along nicely, and the concept revolving around Godstones and Godstones-based magic is a unique one. Elisa is thrown from one adventure into another at a break-neck pace. The author manages to keep your attention on every page and gives no opportunity to get bored. In its pacing this fantasy is very similar to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8306857.Divergent__Divergent___1_" title="Divergent (Divergent, #1) by Veronica Roth" rel="nofollow noopener">Divergent</a>.<br><br>As for the rest, this is the case when I wish some other author wrote this story. There is just something very unripe, maybe even pedestrian about how <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8419564.The_Girl_of_Fire_and_Thorns__Fire_and_Thorns___1_" title="The Girl of Fire and Thorns (Fire and Thorns, #1) by Rae Carson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl of Fire and Thorns</a> is written. It is plagued by rookie flaws.<br><br>First, this novel is a perfect example of what happens when an author is incapable of adhering to the <i>show-not-tell</i> rule. Everything I know about characters, I know because Elisa told me. I know that Elisa is fat, but only because she repeatedly talked about herself like that: "I am fat as a pig. I'll go get me some more cake." I know that her new husband is a coward because she told me so. I know that Elisa is going through internal transformation because Elise told me one day she was fat and stupid and the next day she told me she felt different inside and ready to kill, fight and lead a rebellion. Nothing seems to be revealed in this story through dialog or actions.<br><br>Then, there is a case of romantic-trope loving. For instance, Elisa is married to a stranger in the first chapter. There is a wedding night the same evening and Elisa instantaneously feels she wants "more than a little kiss." Of course, it is a YA novel, so nobody has any sex. (Let me add here, I abhor when authors put their teen characters in situations where logically they would have to have sex, but they don't due to some lame reason. Like here, it is a royal marriage, surely it ought to be consummated. Or like in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8525590.Wither__The_Chemical_Garden___1_" title="Wither (The Chemical Garden, #1) by Lauren DeStefano" rel="nofollow noopener">Wither</a>, where the heroine is kidnapped for the sole purpose of being impregnated, but somehow manages to avoid sex for a year while her husband has no problem sleeping with a 13-year old.) And another example, Elisa is kidnapped and when she sees her kidnapper, her first thoughts are: "I gasp, for his face is only a handspan above mine. I notice his eyes first, huge and glimmering brown like polished bread-nuts. They are framed by more hair than I've ever see on a boy." I am sorry, but aren't you supposed to be scared of your kidnapper? This is not a Harlequin romance, is it?<br><br>There are other things I could latch on to and rant about, but they are more of a personal nature and I think every reader will have to decide for him/herself if it is worth ranting about. These things are: Elisa's fatness and how it is portrayed by the author (IMO, Elisa is the flattest fat person I have ever read about - I have no clue why she overeats, how she feels while overeating and if losing weight was what made her a superhero); and also if this novel should be categorized as Christian lit - the whole story here is basically guided by God and Elisa is a devout believer and prays a lot. Although you can argue that this is a fantasy novel, so it can be any kind of deity, not necessarily a Christian one.<br><br>I would recommend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8419564.The_Girl_of_Fire_and_Thorns__Fire_and_Thorns___1_" title="The Girl of Fire and Thorns (Fire and Thorns, #1) by Rae Carson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl of Fire and Thorns</a> to those who like action-driven books and can overlook deficiencies in character development. For everyone else, I say <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/131936.The_Blue_Sword" title="The Blue Sword by Robin McKinley" rel="nofollow noopener">The Blue Sword</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7012522.The_Queen_of_Attolia__The_Queen_s_Thief___2_" title="The Queen of Attolia (The Queen's Thief, #2) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of Attolia</a> are much better YA fantasy offerings.<br><br>As for me, while I somewhat enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8419564.The_Girl_of_Fire_and_Thorns__Fire_and_Thorns___1_" title="The Girl of Fire and Thorns (Fire and Thorns, #1) by Rae Carson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl of Fire and Thorns</a>'s plot, the lack of swoony teen love or good dialog and a Mary Sue-like main character who succeeds at everything she does, becomes a super-duper warrior queen literally overnight and is loved by everyone will probably stop me from continuing on with this trilogy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4817623502722082745" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1118254829" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1118254829" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1118254829?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1118254829" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2961781533777229838"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“And God raised up for Himself a champion. Yea, once in every four generations He raised him up to bear His mark.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>What better way to take a break from stupid reality things like essays and demanding classes than a YA fantasy book about <b>war, prophecy, an unlikely heroine and mouth-watering food</b>? Ladies and gentlemen, <b>I am pleasantly surprised!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1458939304ra/18552388.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Lucero-Elisa. Heavenly light, chosen of God. His words suffocate me as surely as his embrace. All my life, I've been reminded that I am</i></b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText2961781533777229838" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“And God raised up for Himself a champion. Yea, once in every four generations He raised him up to bear His mark.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>What better way to take a break from stupid reality things like essays and demanding classes than a YA fantasy book about <b>war, prophecy, an unlikely heroine and mouth-watering food</b>? Ladies and gentlemen, <b>I am pleasantly surprised!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1458939304ra/18552388.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Lucero-Elisa. Heavenly light, chosen of God. His words suffocate me as surely as his embrace. All my life, I've been reminded that I am destined for service.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Destined for service she has yet to discover, chosen for an unknown task that will affect her entire world, princess Elisa is trapped in a prison of expectation and ignorance. When she is forced to marry a king she has never met in order to forge a military alliance, she realizes that being solitary and secluded is not an option anymore, that she needs to use her wit to survive in a court full of rivals and save her people from an enemy who has the resources to destroy them, and herself. For it is the Godstone she bears in her belly, the mark of God that everyone is craving that might determine the outcome of the war.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I loved and lost and survived.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4074051.Rae_Carson" title="Rae Carson" rel="nofollow noopener">Rae Carson</a> narrated a <b>different</b> story. The story of a girl who was suffocating under the pressure of being God's chosen one, who had to overcome her insecurities and everybody's mocking and stand up for herself and the ones who needed her. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10429092.The_Girl_of_Fire_and_Thorns__Fire_and_Thorns___1_" title="The Girl of Fire and Thorns (Fire and Thorns, #1) by Rae Carson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl of Fire and Thorns</a> was a <b>coming of age tale</b> that depicted in a realistic, relatable way the struggles of a teenager who ate too much and was not the epitome of beauty or grace, who at first was self-centered and isolated by choice and had to face the real world in order to grow up, become responsible and love herself despite her flaws. <b>Elisa's transformation was astonishing</b>, and Rae's message was plain and simple: <b>first accept yourself and then the others will accept you</b>. All the beauty in the world does not matter if you are rotten inside, if you don't use your brain, if your soul isn't kind.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1446056435ra/16741250.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The world-building and the magic system were painted with bright colours, the religion and each culture unfolded naturally and I absolutely loved the court schemings and the war strategies! There was <b>adventure, intrigue and sorcery</b> and plans that didn't work out that made my heartbeat unsteady and I am pretty sure the next books will be even more gripping! The only thing I didn't enjoy was the romance. Yeah, I can hear your jaw dropping! I found it forced, it lacked of connection and <b>the love interest was rather indifferent</b>. I would be grateful if the next books focused on enigmatic Lord Hector who picked my interest even though I hate moustaches!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452015178ra/17634440.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10429092.The_Girl_of_Fire_and_Thorns__Fire_and_Thorns___1_" title="The Girl of Fire and Thorns (Fire and Thorns, #1) by Rae Carson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl of Fire and Thorns</a> is the first instalment of very promising series about <b>war, destiny, religion and magic</b>, with many interesting characters and an entrancing plotline! I absolutely recommend it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2961781533777229838" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1581649369" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1581649369" />

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1581649369?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1581649369" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4825569185804096083"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458346558i/18477336._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b><u>1.5 stars</u>. All in all incredibly underwhelming and somewhat both idiotic and infuriating.</b> Trust me, I would love to tell you that my distaste <i>only</i> revolves around personal matters - as a strong case of "it's not the book but me", let's say - but in all honesty, <b>I really don't think that</b> and the problems I had with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10429092.The_Girl_of_Fire_and_Thorns__Fire_and_Thorns___1_' title='The Girl of Fire and Thorns (Fire and Thorns, #1) by Rae Carson' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Girl of Fire and Thorns</a> were way too numerous to be left ignored.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"You must not lose faith, child. No matter what. Do not doubt God or his choosing of you. He knows infinitely mo</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText4825569185804096083" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458346558i/18477336._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b><u>1.5 stars</u>. All in all incredibly underwhelming and somewhat both idiotic and infuriating.</b> Trust me, I would love to tell you that my distaste <i>only</i> revolves around personal matters - as a strong case of "it's not the book but me", let's say - but in all honesty, <b>I really don't think that</b> and the problems I had with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10429092.The_Girl_of_Fire_and_Thorns__Fire_and_Thorns___1_" title="The Girl of Fire and Thorns (Fire and Thorns, #1) by Rae Carson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl of Fire and Thorns</a> were way too numerous to be left ignored.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"You must not lose faith, child. No matter what. Do not doubt God or his choosing of you. He knows infinitely more than we can imagine."</i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1492440145i/22517174._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10429092.The_Girl_of_Fire_and_Thorns__Fire_and_Thorns___1_" title="The Girl of Fire and Thorns (Fire and Thorns, #1) by Rae Carson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl of Fire and Thorns</a> can be considered as <b>fast-paced</b>, <i>if you don't mind following characters you don't care about</i> ← I <b>do</b> mind. You know what I also mind? <u>When quantity prevails over quality</u>. Hé, sure, I cannot deny how action-packed the story is <i>but</i> <b>I'd rather read about few in-depth plot points than a succession of superficial twists</b>, because you know what? Wandering around (even in an active fashion) is <b>plain boring</b> all the same. Had the characters stand still for more than 5 pages, perhaps I would have been able to start feeling something. Sadly I didn't.<br><br>Many of my friends loved this book, and because I am naturally trustful (alright, maybe not), I kept reading when I wanted to DNF the hell out of it around 40%. Did it pay off? Huh, not really. Although the plot does pick up in the last 30%, the way events take place stays <b>way too convenient and simple</b> for my liking. <br><br>Not to mention that <b>the writing was terrible</b>, and by that I don't mean grammatical mistakes (there are none that I noticed) - No, I mean that <b>everything was told to me and never ever shown</b>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458346558i/18477338._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>True story</u> : My favorite character is a 5 years-old boy whose appearance doesn't last more than 5 pages. Huh-oh, <b>I may have a problem here.</b> Truth be told, none of these characters were rage-inducing. <i>Nah.</i> They were too busy wandering around, <b>bland and flat as fuck</b>. <br><br>First of all, I'm not sure how <b>Elisa</b> avoided to be called on her Mary Sue status. Is it because she's fat and YA books tend to consider overweight as a synonym of ugly? The girl is God chosen, for crying out loud. Oh, she <i>tells us</i> that she's useless, but then she tells us so many things, I LOST COUNT. Really, though? She gives war advices that get everyone happy, does wonders with children - she even spreads martyr vibes at some point (but on that aspect she improves, woot!). <br><br>I didn't <i>hate</i> Elisa, because I didn't care enough to do so, but it doesn't mean that I liked the way her characterization was handled. <br><br>In my opinion, <b>she conveys a disturbing and infuriating portray of overweight</b>. Look, at first I was really happy to finally see a YA heroine who isn't strikingly beautiful, skinny, and white. <b>So much wasted potential</b> unfortunately. A book isn't body positive when the MC's growth is linked to her lost of weight and when fatness is only seen in a negative light (<i>God forbid</i> that a fat girl be beautiful - yes, there is a pun in there). <br><br>You gotta love pig metaphors, really. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"... as if I am a juicy pig roast garnished with pepper sauce"</i>
</blockquote><br>Seriously. <b>What's up with that?</b> Did I miss a memo? Is it considered as normal and healthy that an overweight MC - one of the only ones I met in YA - constantly self-depreciates herself? Is repeating all over again that she isn't worthy and beautiful because she's not thin serves some purpose I somehow didn't grasp? <br><br>Does she ever realize that her weight - past and present - doesn't begin to define who she is? No, and really, <b>how could she, when the plot never lets any room for that?</b> I do realize that self-loathing can be linked to appearances, especially during the teenage years. <b>I just wish that this important issue had been dealt with more complexity and depth</b>, because as it is, I cannot condone it. <br><br><b>Then come the male-leads</b>. Oh my <i>GOSH</i> what is it with these guys? <br><br>Who the fuck is <b>Lord Hector</b>? His entire characterization is built around the twisting of his moustache. I KID YOU NOT. <br><br>I won't bother talking about <b>the weak husband</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ who doesn't care for telling people they're married and somehow keeps his mistress (who's thin and beautiful, of course).  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Oh, oops, I just did. <br><br>Do not fear, though! Just wait and meet <b>Humberto, the smiling, puppy-like desert man</b> who never convinced me enough to care. <br><br>THESE ARE NOT PEOPLE. <br><br>To be fair, I did enjoy Cosmé and Ximena when they were present, but I still feel as if <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4074051.Rae_Carson" title="Rae Carson" rel="nofollow noopener">Rae Carson</a> only scratched the surface of their personalities, unfortunately. <br><br>And do not get me started about these painted-faced enemies we know nothing about. <b>As a rule, all the villains are plain EVIL, without any nuances. BO-RING.</b><br><br>More generally, I found <u>two ways of dividing the whole set of characters</u> : <br><b>Way #1</b> : The Fat vs. The Beautiful<br><b>Way #2</b> : Those who like Elisa vs. Those who don't like Elisa<br><br>This is the extend of characterization as far as I'm concerned, and <b>I have yet to see some dynamics in there</b> (at this point, I'm not even asking for chemistry).<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458346558i/18477339._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>Again, a fail</u>. <b>Let's talk about the religious stuff, okay?</b> I saw many readers stating that it wasn't Christian at all (but then why not name the god something else, and why make it seem like a Bible parable, and why add some martyr vibes, I wonder), and I'm ready to acknowledge the fact that I have literally no patience for praying and sentences like "god knows all" in my books. Granted, it irks me something fierce in Fantasy, but let's not take my personal taste into account, okay? <br><br>Let's forget that I had to suffer from entire paragraphs like this : <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"My soul glorifies God; let rejoice in my Savior <br>For he has been mindful of his humble servant<br>Blessed am I among generations<br>For he lifted me from the dying world<br>Yea, with his righteous right hand he lifted me<br>He has redeemed his people, given them new life abundant<br>My soul glorifies God; let it rejoice in my Savior."</i>
</blockquote><br>(for full disclosure, I have to point that they're in church at this moment, and this is not the MC talking, but a priest)<br><br>Let's also not mention the constant praying, okay? <u>It still bothers me very much</u>. Why, you ask? <b>Because it may be one of the LAZIEST magical system I've ever read about</b>. What the fuck is this shit, really? So she prays and the God Gemstone in her belly-button helps her .... <i>Sometimes?</i> <br><br>REALLY?! RANDOM MUCH?! I can't believe how easy and idiotic it makes the plot. No explanation needed - because GOD. <i>Pl</i>-ease. Give me a break. <br><br>▶ <i>Sigh</i>. <b>I could go on and on and on, it would remain that I'm in the almost non-existent minority on this one, and sad to be</b>. In all honesty, I know that I can enjoy YA Fantasy, even <i>tropey</i> - I recently read and loved <i>the Seven Realms series</i> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/125308.Cinda_Williams_Chima" title="Cinda Williams Chima" rel="nofollow noopener">Cinda Williams Chima</a>. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10429092.The_Girl_of_Fire_and_Thorns__Fire_and_Thorns___1_" title="The Girl of Fire and Thorns (Fire and Thorns, #1) by Rae Carson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl of Fire and Thorns</a> doesn't compare anywhere near the still predictable <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6342491.The_Demon_King__Seven_Realms___1_" title="The Demon King (Seven Realms, #1) by Cinda Williams Chima" rel="nofollow noopener">The Demon King</a>. And I'm not even talking about the awesomeness of <i>The Lumatere Chronicles</i>.<br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

    <a title="High Lady of The Night Court" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court"><img alt="High Lady of The Night Court" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556501727p2/62560505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1842299165?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="High Lady of The Night Court" class="user" itemprop="url" name="High Lady of The Night Court" href="/user/show/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court">High Lady of The Night Court</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court?shelf=fantasy-read">fantasy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1842299165" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4682600323611995685"><b>
  <i>Truly honorable death, the only honorable death, is one that enables life.</i>
</b><br/><br/>I enjoyed reading this book but not in the way I expected. The characters were very realistic and the concept of the Godstone was very unique. The story moves at a good pace and I look forward to seeing where Rae Carson takes this story. This book, in my opinion, had enough potential to be left as a standalone but there are 2 more books and I am genuinely interested in seeing how our protagonist grows into the position</span>
  <span id="freeText4682600323611995685" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Truly honorable death, the only honorable death, is one that enables life.</i>
</b><br /><br />I enjoyed reading this book but not in the way I expected. The characters were very realistic and the concept of the Godstone was very unique. The story moves at a good pace and I look forward to seeing where Rae Carson takes this story. This book, in my opinion, had enough potential to be left as a standalone but there are 2 more books and I am genuinely interested in seeing how our protagonist grows into the position she reaches at the end of the book. <br /><br />There was definitely a lot growth in the protagonist’s personality but the growth was not unrealistically fast or like an epiphany to think differently, the arc in her personality was fitting because of the hardships she endures which led her to grow as a person. Once I finished the book, I thought back on how our protagonist was thinking about herself and the people around her in the first quarter of the book and the maturity and understanding in her actions and thoughts at the end of the book was miraculous. <br /><br />Our protagonist, Elisa is the bearer of a Godstone, a bearer is chosen once in every century and they are believed to be destined to a litre of service. It's Elisa’s sixteenth birthday which also happens to be the day she is to wed King Alejandro. She believes marrying him and completing this ‘peace treaty’ she was never told about, is her act of service. She is <i>very</i> mistaken. Turns out the people who told her everything she knows about the Godstone were holding out on her. There is so much she has yet to learn about her role as the bearer and the responsibilities that come along with it. There are people out there who want the Godstone from her, and they will stop at nothing to take it from her.<br /><br />Elisa is the bearer of the Godstone, and in that she is blessed, but in every other aspect of her life she believes she remains unimportant. Her sister, Alodia, has always been the favored one, she is the heir to the throne and deals with all the political aspects of her kingdom along with their father. <br />But in the first chapter, it is clear that more than anything Elisa vies for her sister’s competence, grace, and beauty. She is clearly jealous of her sister and in her jealousy she assumes her sister hates her. Watching her become her own person, growing to her full potential is very interesting. She sees past her jealousy of her sister and realises her love for her and accepts it. <br /><br />I enjoyed watching her find people she can trust and making friends(in very unlikely circumstances, mind you). She realizes her true purpose and finds meaning in her life which also paves a path for her to self-acceptance. I look forward to reading more books by Rae Carson and I rate this one 4 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4682600323611995685" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1626751402" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1626751402" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1626751402?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1626751402" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3037799356539117049">I don't know.<br/>I liked some parts of it, but it was weird/draggy/& preachy in parts, too. Guess I'll settle on 3 stars?<br/><br/>First off, the whole stone in the belly button thing was sort of strange...& eventually (when she tried to dig it out) off-putting for me.<br/>I just...ewwww.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462806429i/19046318._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Now, supposedly, she was given the stone by God to help her do something special, but the records of the previous Stone Bearers seemed sketchy at best. Some of them accomplished something, some of them died young, and most of them</span>
  <span id="freeText3037799356539117049" style="display:none">I don't know.<br>I liked some parts of it, but it was weird/draggy/&amp; preachy in parts, too. Guess I'll settle on 3 stars?<br><br>First off, the whole stone in the belly button thing was sort of strange...&amp; eventually (when she tried to dig it out) off-putting for me.<br>I just...ewwww.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462806429i/19046318._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now, supposedly, she was given the stone by God to help her do something special, but the records of the previous Stone Bearers seemed sketchy at best. Some of them accomplished something, some of them died young, and most of them faded into obscurity. So....<br>What's the deal with the friggin stone?!<br>Like most things that <i>God</i> gives, there aren't any instructions that come with it. If something good happens, it's because God and/or the stone heard her prayers, and if something bad happens it was because it furthered God and/or the stone's greater plan. <br><i>*cough*bullshit*cough*</i><br>It's just very hard for me to get behind that way of thinking, so this may be a series more suited to someone with faith in his/her religion.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462807800i/19046563._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As far as the Big Showdown at the end?<br>WTF?!<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Did she actually save everyone with a spinning flower pendant attached to her navel?! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>No. No, no, no!<br>Get the fuck outta here with that bullshit.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462810529ra/19047022.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ok, the ambiguous nature of the stone, the religious aspects, and a weird (I felt) superpower reveal were the biggest drawbacks to this book. <br>BUT.<br>There were several things I quite enjoyed about this one, as well.<br>The <i>main</i> thing was Elisa herself.<br>She wasn't perfect, gorgeous, overly skilled, or particularly good at much. Although, she <i>was</i> intelligent. <br>And I know most of the other reviewers have mentioned it, but I thought it was a nice touch that she was also overweight. Yes, she did end up losing quite a few pounds, but (my opinion) that wasn't a bad thing, since it mentions several times how winded she got when she did stuff. So...yeah. In the beginning she appeared to be a bit unhealthy, and with some diet &amp; exercise <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[due to being kidnapped and forced to walk across the desert, while being on the same rations as the others <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> she lost enough to feel good. I <i>do</i> like the fact that she wasn't a stick figure after she lost the weight, though.<br>Healthy is great, starving to be thin is <i>not</i>.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462811641ra/19047290.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I was also happily taken in with the complexity of Elisa's relationships. Everything felt very layered and <i>real</i> when it came to the characters and their motivations. Even her husband and his odd insistence on (and her agreement to!) their strange secret marriage felt plausible under the circumstances.<br>Well done, Ms. Carson!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462814165ra/19047677.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So. While I wasn't blown away, I'm semi-interested in finding out how everything turns out. I'm kinda waffling on picking up the next book, but if nothing better comes along...</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="3037799356539117049" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1455725928" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1455725928" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1455725928?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/13624038-the-girl-of-fire-and-thorns">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=fantastic-lit-and-co">fantastic-lit-and-co</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1455725928" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14414336665061367040"><b>"God's will. How many times have I heard someone declare their understanding of this thing I find so indefinable?"</b><br/><br/>Sometimes it's fascinating how authors can synthesize their own books in just one sentence strategically hidden in the books themselves. Hats off. <br/><br/>•One of the main complaints readers usually have when it comes to this book is <b>the main character</b>. In all honesty, Elisa may be difficult to stand, especially because, especially at the beginning, her way of thinking is strictly linked to<b> </b></span>
  <span id="freeText14414336665061367040" style="display:none"><b>"God's will. How many times have I heard someone declare their understanding of this thing I find so indefinable?"</b><br /><br />Sometimes it's fascinating how authors can synthesize their own books in just one sentence strategically hidden in the books themselves. Hats off. <br /><br />•One of the main complaints readers usually have when it comes to this book is <b>the main character</b>. In all honesty, Elisa may be difficult to stand, especially because, especially at the beginning, her way of thinking is strictly linked to<b> her being overweight</b>. Basically, she's a whining ball of self-pity 90% of the time -as I said, though, as the story proceeds things get a lot better in this respect. I <i>was</i> bothered by Elisa's pity parties, yes, but not particularly (between you and me, my physical constitution is not on the slim side and I had and have to struggle to stay in some kind of shape. So, maybe I empathized? Probably. She can be very irritating, though). Moreover, I would have liked to see her gain some trust in herself while she was still fat, instead it felt like the fact that she lost some weight served as a kind of watershed between wimp Elisa and heroine Elisa. I know the author didn't want to convey such at all, but that's how I felt about it. <br /><br />•But again, how she dealt with her weight is not the main problem -or anyway, it wasn't <i>my</i> main problem. No, my main problem, with the protagonist and with the whole book in general, was <b>Elisa's insufferable self-righteousness</b>. <br />Practical examples:<br /><br /><b>"And then comes the most dreadful thought of all: <i>Is it possible, then, that God would choose bearers among the enemy?"</i></b><br /><br />or<br /><br /><b>"It's God's will."<br />I almost stab him right then. What would this man know of God's will? He is insane, hardly human [...] my enemy presumes to know the mind of God."</b><br /><br /><i>or</i>, and this one is the most disgusting of all,<br /><br /><b>"They were locked inside that building," he says in a wavery voice. "They were left to burn."<br />"Oh, God." The cruelty of it is unfathomable."</b><br /><br />I'm sorry, so no one remembers that she did <i>the very same thing</i> to the man of quote 2, knocking him out, setting fire to his tent, and leaving him in the tent? <i>No one</i>?<br />After reading (many) things like these, I was sure she was going to start shouting "Kill the infidels!" any moment. She's so pious, so moral, so pristine, and then <b>she can't even <i>consider</i> that God is also on the side of someone that's <i>not</i> her</b>. I'm sure many, many colonizers thought the very same things. Thus, sorry, but I am pretty appalled. <br /><br />•Also, <b>she solves pretty much anything by praying it away</b>. I'm not saying she can't be smart and self-sufficient when she wants, but as soon as a problem arises her first thought is "Please God make it right". Mmmh okay? Even though that makes for a very <b>lazy magic system</b> since sometimes it works and that's pretty much all there's to it? <br /><b>This is not a book about religion (which I think it's supposed to be, among other things); this is merely a book <i>with</i> religion</b>. Its role, though pivotal, I guess, is passive. Religion is not properly trotted into play, it is not questioned or pondered or reflected upon. It's there, it says there: be happy with it as it is.<br /><br />•I absolutely do not condone this horrid things authors usually do when they<b> introduce a character only to kill him for the sake of drama</b>. If there's something I hate, that's it: bending the rules of a good storytelling to <i>drama</i>. Please. Like, <i>please</i>. But the funniest thing was, I wasn't even surprised because it was so obvious that's how it was going to go. Wait, no, there's something even funnier: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Humberto appears when Hector leaves the stage and is killed moments before Hector comes back <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Like, you're no one without a love interest around, Elisa. Because again you need an external acknowledgement since you feel ugly <i>et cetera</i>. Again, I can't help finding that a little degrading, even though I'm perfectly aware that the author wanted to propose a heroine completely different from what I perceived. Though, if I did not perceive the right way (if I perceived her <i>so</i> wrongly) something is probably amiss. <br /><br />•As for the rest, there's really not much to say. <b>The plot</b> does its job without being particularly outstanding, and honestly some parts actually saw me bored out of my mind. <b>The characters</b> are average too, with Elisa's exception (a let-me-punch-her exception), while <b>the world-building</b>, as I said, I found rather lacking. <br /><br />➽ Now the question is: <b>will I continue </b>the trilogy? <b>Probably</b>. Many of my friends keep telling me <i>The Crown of Embers</i> is <i>so</i> much better, and I truly am curious, because even though I don't give a fig for the characters, I've got a soft spot for strong-willed and determined heroines (okay: I like them when they are downright fierce and also <s>totally</s> cold-hearted) and Elisa's development does bode well. <b>Fingers crossed</b>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14414336665061367040" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=romance">romance</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=recommended-to-me">recommended-to-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=shawty-so-bad">shawty-so-bad</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1679349694" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6245233358685601621">3.5 stars<br/><br/>This book was weird. It so boring at times yet somewhat enjoyable. The only reason I was able to enjoy this was because of that romance. Seriously, what the fuck happened, I'm <i>still screaming.</i><br/><br/>Here are some reasons why I liked this book:<br/><br/>◇<b>We don't have a skinny MC</b>. I love how Elisa wasn't a skinny heroine and what she looks like shouldn't matter. She was smart, brave, thought and extremely fucking annoying at times and I loved it. <br/><br/>◇I loved how Humberto treated her. He fell in love with he</span>
  <span id="freeText6245233358685601621" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br />This book was weird. It so boring at times yet somewhat enjoyable. The only reason I was able to enjoy this was because of that romance. Seriously, what the fuck happened, I'm <i>still screaming.</i><br /><br />Here are some reasons why I liked this book:<br /><br />◇<b>We don't have a skinny MC</b>. I love how Elisa wasn't a skinny heroine and what she looks like shouldn't matter. She was smart, brave, thought and extremely fucking annoying at times and I loved it. <br /><br />◇I loved how Humberto treated her. He fell in love with her because <b>of her personality</b> and he didn't care that she was fat, which seriously shouldn't matter. <br /><br />◇The romance. SERIOUS SPOILER. DO NOT OPEN IF YOU HAVEN'T READ THE BOOK. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[this is the first book where both of the fucking love interests die. hats off to you Rae Carson. well done <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />◇<b>This book has God in it</b>. Which was very weird at first, but then I got used to it and was pretty normal about it. It's weird seeing God in a YA Fantasy book. I'm religious and it <b>was very weird at first</b> because it's not something we read about everyday. But I'm glad to see a book where God plays an impact. It isn't even preachy so that's great.<br /><br />What I didn't like:<br /><br />◇The fucking plot. The plot takes a completely new turn in the second half of this book, like what the fuck is even going on. Slow down, I'm dumb, let me process all this, thanks. <br /><br />◇This was very boring and slow at times??? Like I was ready to DNF this around 200 pages BUT THEN HUMBERTO CAME IN AND SAVED THE DAY.<br /><br />This was a great read and I'd like to read the sequel. <br /></span>

<div id="review_2053605701" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2053605701" />
    <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance"><img alt="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513125058p2/68538597.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2053605701?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance">❄️BooksofRadiance❄️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68538597-booksofradiance?shelf=ya-fantasy-sci-fi">ya-fantasy-sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2053605701" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12885295947523620317"><b>10/12/17</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1512962844ra/24651279.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Help, I feel… nothing.<br/><br/>You know when you can’t say you hated or loved a book because you can't even remember what went on? That's how I feel right now. I don’t remember half the characters much less the plot because I was so bored and I’ve only finished it just a few hrs ago. 🤦‍♀️<br/>Pray you don't feel the dread of indifference, my friends because a lack of any emotion towards a book is far worse than hating it. At least then you still feel… something.<br/>However, all’s not doom and gloom becaus</span>
  <span id="freeText12885295947523620317" style="display:none"><b>10/12/17</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1512962844ra/24651279.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Help, I feel… nothing.<br><br>You know when you can’t say you hated or loved a book because you can't even remember what went on? That's how I feel right now. I don’t remember half the characters much less the plot because I was so bored and I’ve only finished it just a few hrs ago. 🤦‍♀️<br>Pray you don't feel the dread of indifference, my friends because a lack of any emotion towards a book is far worse than hating it. At least then you still feel… something.<br>However, all’s not doom and gloom because I’m not heartbroken over my disappointment as I went into this not because I expected to be blown away but to get to the second book. If <b>THAT </b> ends up disappointing me, then I’ll simply have to punch someone. <br><br>Anyhow, let's get to it.<br>Lucero-Elisa’s a reluctant, plus-size princess of Oravalle, who was born with a Godstone in her belly. A mark that comes only once a century - a sign that she’s marked out by divinity for a great destiny. Told in the first person narrative, we’re sucked right into Elisa’s world as the story opens on the day of her marriage to King Alejandro of a neighbouring kingdom, Joya d’Arena, for a political allegiance.<br>After the marriage, she sets off to her husband’s kingdom and… this is where it all falls apart.<br> <br>The mystery element of the book was completely lost on me because I found nothing mysterious about it and the characters were simply too boring to remember. The other issue I had was that many of the conflicts were resolved too quickly and far too conveniently. It was one of those plots where it’s so predictable that you knew how it ended before it even began.<br><br><br><b>WHAT I LOVED:</b><br><br>Though I was extremely underwhelmed by the plot, Elisa was the redeeming factor of this book (and why I gave it 3 stars). I. Loved. Her. <br>As intelligent as she is, Elisa’s insecurities seep through the pages. Right from the beggining, she had the odds stacked against her - married and shipped off to a strange land, carying the weight and responsibilities of being the Godstone bearer, which put her in constant danger, she has serious insecurity about her appearance and considers herself to be fat &amp; ugly and is very self deprecating - When we first meet her, struggling to fit into her wedding dress, she compares herself to a sausage and hopes that her unseen husband will be ugly, or old to protect herself from his inevitable disgust. Moreover, once outside the walls of her own country, she experiences the horror of battle, of betrayal and of loss but through it all, she never once complains or gives up. <br>Hallelujah! A YA heroine who isn't whiny! Instead, using her intelligence, she tries to find a way through the innumerable challenges thrown in her path and over the course of the novel, Elisa grows into her own and blossoms from uncertain and self-doubting girl to a capable and respected leader.<br><br>While this book fell short on many levels (I’ve always had issues with first books and this was no exception) I do plan on continuing with the series. I am nothing if not an optimist and <b>Hopefully</b> I’ll have better luck with the next one.<br><br><br><br><b>7/12/17</b><br><br>I’ve heard so many mixed reviews for this book and the curiosity is killing me, so, I’m going to give it a try and judge for myself.<br><br>Here goes...</span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText12995937091392453872" style="display:none">Oh, my goodness.<br /><br />A heroine who actually thinks for herself?<br />A heroine who doesn't get swayed by hot men?<br />A heroine who overcomes her fears realistically and courageously?<br />A heroine who is perfect in her imperfections?<br />A heroine who is flawed yet so real?<br /><br /><b>A FANTASY STORY WHERE THE ROMANCE IS ACTUALLY NOT CENTRAL???</b><br /><br />Ooh. La. <b>Freaking</b>. La.<br /><br />To say that I enjoyed this book is an understatement.<br /><br />It's been a while since I finished a book in one sitting. Seriously, recently, it takes me 3-5 days max to finish a single book. This one woke me up from that horrendous daze and made me remember why reading is so enjoyable.<br /><br />And yes, if you haven't picked up the hint, this is to say you have to read this book now if you haven't yet. Now, now, <b>now!</b></span>
