<div id="review_855244606" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/855244606" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/855244606?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=foodie-fiction">foodie-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer855244606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1387973524093155335"><b>I am <i>ridiculously</i> in love with this book.</b> I've been gnawing at fantasies like a fiend lately and FINALLY I found this one which is a) unique, and b) feministic, and c) incredibly adorable and charming and heart warming. WELL. Apart from the moments when my heart was <i>breaking</i>. This author does NOT spare her characters. AHHH. WHERE EVEN TO BEGIN?!!<br/><br/><b>It's an incredible rich fantasy world, which was gorgeous to eat.</b> My only single complaint was that it was a bit hard to pin-point all the countries and</span>
  <span id="freeText1387973524093155335" style="display:none"><b>I am <i>ridiculously</i> in love with this book.</b> I've been gnawing at fantasies like a fiend lately and FINALLY I found this one which is a) unique, and b) feministic, and c) incredibly adorable and charming and heart warming. WELL. Apart from the moments when my heart was <i>breaking</i>. This author does NOT spare her characters. AHHH. WHERE EVEN TO BEGIN?!!<br /><br /><b>It's an incredible rich fantasy world, which was gorgeous to eat.</b> My only single complaint was that it was a bit hard to pin-point all the countries and who-was-at-war-with-who. (But that could be just me.) The world is BIG though, which I loved. And I think it was Italian-inspired?! Whatever it was it wasn't Britain so THAT was refreshing too.<br /><br /><b>But we haaave to talk about CHARACTERS.</b> Basically: Elisa. If nothing else: read this book for the incredibleness that is Elisa. Her character development is MARVELLOUS. I'm reeling. I am. She's an unconfident child in the beginning and a insanely clever queen at the end. She also has an eating disorder which was wonderful. I mean, not that the disorder is wonderful, but just the fact that it's DIVERSE and FABULOUS. And also how Elisa liked pastries. I mean...YUM. *ahem* But wooowowow. I just...I really admired and looked up to Elisa. She definitely goes down as one of the BEST characters I've ever read.<br /><br />-<b>Alejandro:</b> Totally a weak sap head. I mean, who marries a girl and then proceeds to pretend you didn't?!! WHAT IS WRONG WITH HIM.<br />-<b> Xemina:</b> Freaky, but awesome. She killed a dude with a hairpin. Also a bodyguard/nurse.<br />-<b>Cosme:</b> She was a pleasant surprise! I thought she was just going to be a snooty maid, but noooo she turned out INCREDIBLE and so multi-layered. <br /><b>- Rosario:</b> He's the little 6-year-old prince and an absolute BRAT but so adoralb.e <br /><b>- Hector:</b> OH HEEEECTOR. He didn't have the most massive role in the book, but I totally shipped him and Elisa. I DID. <br /><b>-Hecberto:</b> He was a hesitant love interest, but more importantly part of the rebel army. I gotta admit, I didn't love him. But <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I definitely wilted when he died. THROAT SLIT IN FRONT OF ELISA. I mean....woah. It was super sad and I might've been clutching the pages hissing nasty things at the enemy at that point. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Basically I LOVE the characters, with barely any of them letting me odwn. My only complaint is their names. Like: what even. <br /><br /><b>THE WRITING IS JUST GREAT.</b> Like, it's a bit long and wordy. The beginning isn't fast. Actually, the whole book isn't astronomically fast, and I did feel a bit weary reading it. But Elisa has such a winning voice, I couldn't mind too much. And though I wish it'd warpped up faster, I STILL LOVED IT. <br /><br /><b>MY ONLY COMPLAINTS:</b><br /><b>+ It's very heavily dependant on religion.</b> Eh, I dunno, peoples. I'm just not a fan of religion in books. <br /><b>+ It was long.</b> Too long? I mean, it's not an exhausting word count (440pgs) but it was very detailed and I had to REALLY focus to read which I find hard. <br /><b>+ Elisa has a "godstone" stuck in her stomach and I hoped for more magic.</b> It as totally reasonable that there WASN'T more more magic and the book sort of addressed that, buuuuut. I wish there had been less time listening to boring prayers and more time discovering what the godstone did/was.<br /><b>+ Um..the title?!</b> It really doesn't fit. SORRY. I just wish the title had been less majestic and more in line with the story.<br /><br /><br /><b>ALSO I GOTTA TAKE A MOMENT FOR THE AUTHOR'S NOTE.</b> It. was. incredible. It was about sexism in the workplace and what inspired the author to delve into eating disorders in her epic fantasy and how she handled over-weight issues and her fears that her intentions with Elisa's weight gain/loss could be misconstrued. It was a simply incredible note, okay?! And so. so. true. I'm very passionate about feminism and I LOVED that this book tackled it head on. And it wasn't suffocatingly oppressive. Ergh, I read books all the time where the sexism is stifling (even if the book is addressing the issue, the world is just so crappy) but <i>A Girl of Fire And Thorns</i> had sexism in there, but Elisa wasn't spending 100% of the time convincing people of her worth "even though she was a woman". She was learning about confidence and self-image. I JUST ADMIRE THIS AUTHOR A LOT. This is one of the <i>best</i> debuts ever.<br /><br />Okay. OKAY. I'm gonna go sit in my corner and hug the book now. And then cry a little because of the deaths and the beautiful character development and the gut-twisting ending and....and...THE FEELING OF "I-NEED-BOOK-2-NOW" THAT IS WRITHING IN MY BRAIN. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1387973524093155335" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_178266387" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/178266387" />
    <a title="tonya." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4358824-tonya"><img alt="tonya." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350794820p2/4358824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/178266387?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="tonya." class="user" itemprop="url" name="tonya." href="/user/show/4358824-tonya">tonya.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4358824-tonya?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4358824-tonya?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4358824-tonya?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4358824-tonya?shelf=poc">poc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4358824-tonya?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer178266387" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12349145375115572282">This was one of those books I have a hard time rating, simply because some elements were very well done, and others very poorly done.<br/><br/><i>The Girl of Fire and Thorns</i> is the story of Elisa, princess to the country of Oravalle and bearer of the Godstone, a jewel implanted in her navel that signifies she is marked by god as one who will do a Service. Elisa has no idea what her Service will be, and can't imagine herself ever being useful to her country. She is merely the overweight, shy younger daughter </span>
  <span id="freeText12349145375115572282" style="display:none">This was one of those books I have a hard time rating, simply because some elements were very well done, and others very poorly done.<br /><br /><i>The Girl of Fire and Thorns</i> is the story of Elisa, princess to the country of Oravalle and bearer of the Godstone, a jewel implanted in her navel that signifies she is marked by god as one who will do a Service. Elisa has no idea what her Service will be, and can't imagine herself ever being useful to her country. She is merely the overweight, shy younger daughter of the King, overshadowed in every way by her cunning and charming sister. Her life consists of reading and eating... until she is forced to marry the King of the neighboring country in order to strengthen their alliance and build a greater army against their common enemy: the Invierne. What follows is her transformation from dispassionate, useless girl to a hero.<br /><br />In theory, anyway.<br /><br />Though the writing and premise was strong and engaging, the entire novel was nearly ruined for me by the protagonist's personality in the first two-thirds of the book. While I do give credit to Carson for creating a main character who is not slender and beautiful and lusted after by every male in the story, I wish she had made Elisa stronger. I could relate at times to her emotional overeating and her feelings of unworthiness, but it was overdone to the point of annoyance. Elisa's weight and relationship with food should not have taken the place of personality, but it was nearly all we got. <br /><br />Though Elisa did eventually become a strong character, the fact that it was not until she'd lost weight was offensive, in my opinion. She was educated and knowledgeable in war time strategy, could she not have been a strong force from the beginning? I understand character arcs, but her weight loss <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[through wandering the desert for days with injuries and little food <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> as the catalyst for her transformation was insulting. And frankly, though I am not one to believe that young people are so impressionable that books could sway them in a negative direction, I think this book sends the wrong message to young girls.<br /><br />However, if you are looking for a good fantasy read, I do see potential in the series moving forward. By the end of the book, Elisa had developed into a strong, mostly likable character. And though there are two more books in the series, <i>The Girl of Fire and Thorns</i> was a complete story, with few lingering threads at its end. <br /><br />2.5 stars, rounding up to three in good faith for the rest of the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12349145375115572282" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer502767576" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15068082877716479155"><b>Reread time with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow-rabid-reads-no-more' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jessica</a></b><br/><br/>*chanting* <i>please hold up, please hold up. please hold up.</i> I loved this series the first time through. So lets do it all again. I'm really hoping it is just as good.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515160127ra/24836101.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Whew and it did hold up well. I'm going to stick with my 4 star rating and since I knew some of the bigger plot points I was able to focus in a little more on a certain Captain of the Guard. Hector, you are amazing.<br/><br/><b>Original Review </b><br/><br/>I will preface that I was a little worried about this book when I started. It se</span>
  <span id="freeText15068082877716479155" style="display:none"><b>Reread time with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow-rabid-reads-no-more" rel="nofollow noopener">Jessica</a></b><br><br>*chanting* <i>please hold up, please hold up. please hold up.</i> I loved this series the first time through. So lets do it all again. I'm really hoping it is just as good.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515160127ra/24836101.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Whew and it did hold up well. I'm going to stick with my 4 star rating and since I knew some of the bigger plot points I was able to focus in a little more on a certain Captain of the Guard. Hector, you are amazing.<br><br><b>Original Review </b><br><br>I will preface that I was a little worried about this book when I started. It seemed like there would be some religious intonations and sometimes that can get a bit preachy and be a total turn off for me. I will say that wasn’t the case at all. The Godstone is a part of the story but Elisa is the story. I can truthfully say I never felt preached to or at.<br><br>The book starts out with the wedding of a princess to a prince. But she isn’t your normal princess or heroine in books. She is timid, fat and so unsure of herself. Elisa was born with a Godstone in her bellybutton and that means that she has a destiny, she has been chosen. But, Elisa doesn’t feel special or chosen and has no idea why this honor was bestowed upon her especially when her sister is the one it seems to have all the beauty and talent. She is married off to a man she has never met and whisked away to his country. This is where the action begins, because even the journey is treacherous. The caravan is attacked on the way to Elisa’s new home and she has her first opportunity in the presence of danger to shine.<br><br>I loved Elisa in this book, she grew so much. In the beginning she was a little hard to love as a main character because she seemed so weak and pampered finding comfort in food. But right away she starts to grow into her own and become a woman from the little girl she was. I was so intrigued by what the godstone meant and why everyone is trying to hide that Elisa bears it. She has studied the art of war and religious texts all of her life in preparation for whatever her destiny is. She became very interesting and after meeting the rest of the supporting characters I was hooked. Her Journey through this book was fantastic; she was brave and used her mind to win the battles she faced. I think that it was really telling of the characters that recognized her after her transformation; those are the people that really loved her, saw her.<br><br>Once I finished the book I couldn’t wait to start the next book in the series. I wanted more time with all the characters. Fantastic first book.</span>

<div id="review_1353131432" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1353131432" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1353131432?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=boooring">boooring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=when-sparks-don-t-fly">when-sparks-don-t-fly</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=not-as-good-as-i-expected">not-as-good-as-i-expected</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=i-spy-something-pointy">i-spy-something-pointy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=insta-love-add-water">insta-love-add-water</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=oh-my-god">oh-my-god</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1353131432" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13915615341767862274"><b>DNF at 50%</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"I understand why it is better to die from my service than never complete it at all. Far, far better. Homer and Damian never profited from their acts of heroism; everyone who followed did. In the same way, I may never reap the benefits of mine, should I complete it. But that doesn't matter, because God placing his stone in my belly was never about me."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449826031ra/17345183.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I firmly believe a new genre should be carved out just for The Girl of Fire and Thorns: <b>Religious Fantasy.</b> Lord, is it preachy—just </span>
  <span id="freeText13915615341767862274" style="display:none"><b>DNF at 50%</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I understand why it is better to die from my service than never complete it at all. Far, far better. Homer and Damian never profited from their acts of heroism; everyone who followed did. In the same way, I may never reap the benefits of mine, should I complete it. But that doesn't matter, because God placing his stone in my belly was never about me."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449826031ra/17345183.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I firmly believe a new genre should be carved out just for The Girl of Fire and Thorns: <b>Religious Fantasy.</b> Lord, is it preachy—just look at some of these quotes: "The Scriptura Sancta says that all men are equal in the sight of God" or "My soul glorifies God; let it rejoice in my Savior".<br><br>There's nothing wrong with incorporating religion in fictional universes. But when it bears a remarkable resemblance to a religion that currently exists in our world, you start to wonder what the book's agenda is. (Every book promotes some sort of message or value. Those that cry "It's just fiction!" and has no impact on our world at all are just deluding themselves.) <br><br>Again, overt religion does not equal bad. Simply, from my heathen agnostic perspective, it doesn't make for enjoyable reading. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1507371724ra/24110578.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>I liked the main character, Elisa.</b> In fact, I cheered when I saw that she was fat and unabashedly portrayed as such. Some reviewers have mentioned that she's defined by her "fatness" and though I see where they're coming from, I thought it was refreshing to have a YA heroine is self-conscious about her weight, yet also loves eating (admittedly sometimes as a form of therapy). At the same thing, she's the Chosen One, and is battle strategy-savvy and uses it to make up for her shortcomings. <br><br>As someone who's naturally thin, however, I'm ready to concede my perspective is flawed. And Elisa does thin down later in the plot, which is implied as beauty. So take this point with healthy skepticism.<br><br>There's a love triangle, which I saw coming a light year away. Nothing really special, just your typical royalty vs. peasant duel. <br><br>Final verdict—Papa don't preach. Do it somewhere else.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13915615341767862274" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The premise was interesting and unique and I felt many different feels while reading this story. <br/><br/>I would also like to note that (for me anyway) the synopsis does not do this book justice at all. I really expected this to be more of a fluff fantasy and I ended up putting it off for so long because of it. <br/><br/>Very much looking forward to continuing!</span>

<div id="review_561018713" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/561018713" />
    <a title="Victoria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1228180-victoria"><img alt="Victoria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474331741p2/1228180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/561018713?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victoria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victoria" href="/user/show/1228180-victoria">Victoria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1228180-victoria?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer561018713" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4810359186275122681">How many fat, introverted, intellectual princesses do we have in YA fantasy lit—-or any fiction, for that matter? I appreciate that Rae Carson went to the effort of writing against type. Despite noble efforts, though, this book is just a pile of fail.<br/><br/>What made me angry with this book? Let me count the ways:<br/><br/>1. Fat hate: I'm sure that overweight readers (especially those who have issues with binging) will identify with Elisa, but I'm really fucking exhausted of every overweight central character i</span>
  <span id="freeText4810359186275122681" style="display:none">How many fat, introverted, intellectual princesses do we have in YA fantasy lit—-or any fiction, for that matter? I appreciate that Rae Carson went to the effort of writing against type. Despite noble efforts, though, this book is just a pile of fail.<br /><br />What made me angry with this book? Let me count the ways:<br /><br />1. Fat hate: I'm sure that overweight readers (especially those who have issues with binging) will identify with Elisa, but I'm really fucking exhausted of every overweight central character in any book ever (and I can only think of three, yeesh) having an overeating disorder. It's simplistic at best and insulting at worst.<br /><br />2. Weight loss equated with the protagonist coming into her own: Of course, Princess Elisa loses a ton of weight when she's captured by rebels, forced to walk across a desert for a month, and then compelled to lead the rebel forces in battle. Sigh.<br /><br />3. Weight loss equated with heroism: Almost no one respects Elisa until she loses weight. It's presented as coincidental--she hasn't done anything yet to merit respect--but frankly, you're writing a book for teens. Don't do shit like that.<br /><br />4. Jungle savages: There's an attack early in the book by jungle savages with "evil" tattoos etc. etc. Yes, Ms. Carson, this is racism.<br /><br />5. Stockholm syndrome equated with romance: So, the rebels that captured Elisa and brought her over to their side in the war? Naturally, there's a young, handsome man among them who looks out for her when she's helpless and who eventually becomes the romantic interest. We're teaching young women that they should look for a charmer who kidnaps them, then? (Enough of Twilight already.)<br /><br />6. Shyness as an obstacle to worth: There's an underlying message here that while Elisa was shy and avoided the spotlight, she was useless. She's only valuable, only worthy of respect, once she starts taking action and leading the rebels. Introverts, sensitive sorts, and shy kids—you're not welcome here, either.<br /><br />Grrrrrrr.<br /><br />Dear author, not every fat girl has an eating disorder. Not every fat girl needs to be kidnapped out of her bed, forced to walk for a month in the desert, and conveniently find her inner skinny chick in the course of becoming the hero she is supposed to be—-even as she obsesses over food and her weight on virtually every single page. Every. Page.<br /><br />Elisa saves the day on brains and stubbornness. While the book is eminently readable and Elisa is more humanly flawed than most protagonists, I had to force my way through against the downright frustrating, annoying, and bigoted characterization.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4810359186275122681" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2172190805" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2172190805" />
    <a title="Shelly Strange" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25393430-shelly-strange"><img alt="Shelly Strange" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600285315p2/25393430.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2172190805?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelly Strange" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelly Strange" href="/user/show/25393430-shelly-strange">Shelly Strange</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=gurrrl-power">gurrrl-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy-witches-and-wizards">fantasy-witches-and-wizards</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2172190805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15056891914530924702"><b>3.5 stars</b> <br/><br/>Crappy Review Time - This takes place in a sort of reimagined Spanish country with a big splash of desert terrain mixed in. So you've got the adobe villas along with camels and sand storms. The background is religious: every century, "God" (it seems to be a Catholic-y god, but is also kind of undefined), chooses a "bearer" to wear a magic stone in their belly button. The stone appears in infancy and is attached until death. We aren't really sure what the stone does for awhile, but it h</span>
  <span id="freeText15056891914530924702" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b> <br /><br />Crappy Review Time - This takes place in a sort of reimagined Spanish country with a big splash of desert terrain mixed in. So you've got the adobe villas along with camels and sand storms. The background is religious: every century, "God" (it seems to be a Catholic-y god, but is also kind of undefined), chooses a "bearer" to wear a magic stone in their belly button. The stone appears in infancy and is attached until death. We aren't really sure what the stone does for awhile, but it has magic, and the bearer is chosen to do some special deed.<br /><br />The main character is a teen and is married off right away to an older man. They never consummate the marriage (it is YA after all), and there is another semi-romantic interest as well. You get a bit of the rag tag misfits trope. <br /><br />Overall, the story was good! The main character is "fat" in the beginning. Like sausagey fat, not just a little round. But she loses weight and ends up kicking ass. I guess she had to lose the weight to walk around in all that sand. Realism and all that. But, she was likable and grew and I appreciate that. I guess she might be a bit of a Mary Sue and Special Snowflake, but she also had to work for it and not EVERYONE liked her immediately.<br /><br />I think I will continue. I can understand why some thought this was too religious or preachy, since prayer and religion plays a fairly significant part. I just skimmed over those parts. :)<br /><br />A lot happens and it was well-paced. I clicked with the writing style enough to want to see what happens next.<br /><br />(Man, what a generic review, lol. Gots to move on, no time to make it speshul, sorry.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="15056891914530924702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_930813607" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/930813607" />
    <a title="Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2544584-lauren"><img alt="Lauren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442501340p2/2544584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/930813607?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren" href="/user/show/2544584-lauren">Lauren</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer930813607" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17997398950478121704">WE NEED DIVERSE BOOKS<br/><br/>There is a special place in my heart for fantasy novels. I love getting lost in a world that exists only because one person dreamed it. There’s nothing more exciting than starting a new book that feels different from anything you’ve read before. <br/><br/>Immediately, I knew that The Girl of Fire and Thorns was one such book. As it opens, the protagonist, Elisa, is worried about fitting into her wedding dress, and praying that her husband will be ugly because she’s so worried she’ll d</span>
  <span id="freeText17997398950478121704" style="display:none">WE NEED DIVERSE BOOKS<br /><br />There is a special place in my heart for fantasy novels. I love getting lost in a world that exists only because one person dreamed it. There’s nothing more exciting than starting a new book that feels different from anything you’ve read before. <br /><br />Immediately, I knew that The Girl of Fire and Thorns was one such book. As it opens, the protagonist, Elisa, is worried about fitting into her wedding dress, and praying that her husband will be ugly because she’s so worried she’ll disappoint him. YA frequently deals with the anxiety of not feeling accepted, with feelings of not fitting in, but it is rare to see a novel that unflinchingly describes the very real exclusion and ridicule that Elisa is subjected to from her community. <br /><br />It’s also a story that completely flips the racial dichotomy that has become attached to high fantasy novels, at least since Lord of the Rings, where the good guys are associated with white, and the villain’s otherness is synonymous with blackness and dark. I don’t want to spoil too much… but Carson has built a fantasy world that defies expectations, genre conventions, and challenges our perceptions of race and the body head on.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17997398950478121704" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/685550244" />
    <a title="Rusty&#39;s Ghost Engine (also known as.......... Jinky Spring)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21530568-rusty-s-ghost-engine-also-known-as-jinky-spring"><img alt="Rusty&#39;s Ghost Engine (also known as..........   <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/685550244?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rusty&#39;s Ghost Engine (also known as.......... Jinky Spring)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rusty&#39;s Ghost Engine (also known as.......... Jinky Spring)" href="/user/show/21530568-rusty-s-ghost-engine-also-known-as-jinky-spring">Rusty&#39;s Ghost Engine (also known as.......... Jinky Spring)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21530568-rusty-s-ghost-engine-also-known-as-jinky-spring?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21530568-rusty-s-ghost-engine-also-known-as-jinky-spring?shelf=hell-yeah">hell-yeah</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer685550244" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5086951725181633875">3.5 stars <br/><br/><b>SPOILER ALERT...</b><br/><br/>Well I don't think I've ever read a book where both the heroines love interests die.. who will she spend forever with now?<br/><br/>The storyline of this book is basically about a princess trying to find out what her role is as a bearer and trying to find a way to save her country from inland enemies who want access to the port for whatever reasons and will stop at nothing to get it. It was never answered why the enemy wanted a complete collection of godstones or why they so desp</span>
  <span id="freeText5086951725181633875" style="display:none">3.5 stars <br /><br /><b>SPOILER ALERT...</b><br /><br />Well I don't think I've ever read a book where both the heroines love interests die.. who will she spend forever with now?<br /><br />The storyline of this book is basically about a princess trying to find out what her role is as a bearer and trying to find a way to save her country from inland enemies who want access to the port for whatever reasons and will stop at nothing to get it. It was never answered why the enemy wanted a complete collection of godstones or why they so desperately wanted rights to the docks they only said it was gods will for what they were doing. <br /><br />There was plenty of thrill in the writing and narrative and I loved the descriptions of the desert and Elisa's struggles to adapt to an un pampered life. Yet despite all the hardships thrown at her from the start of her kidnap she was unspoiled and only complained about serious vital things e.g. Lack of food and water. She was never vain and never complained about trivial things like her hair or lack of service etc. I did get on with her yet have got to admit felt a little detached from her and the characters through lack of emotions shown. This was only a small glitch though.<br /><br />There was world building but it was a little scarce in my opinion. It described how god rescued humankind by bringing them into that world in his right hand. It also described how Elisa 's people left the country of Joya to colonise the valleys because they thought joya had strayed from the path of god and they intended to peruse god by studying the sacred texts. There was the description of how a bearer is chosen every century at their naming ceremony when the blue godstone appears with light in their navel. All bearers are chosen by god to perform an act of heroism for him and although it appeared that many bearers didn't complete their service it was thought at the end that all the bearers contributed in little ways to one large deed and Elisa has yet to play her part.<br /><br />I was quite surprised with the ending though I mean how could the author kill off two important characters....<br /><br />I did enjoy the action and unpredictability of this book and look forward to the rest of the series. I would recommend this book to those who are looking for a high fantasy that keeps one guessing and has a different cultural feel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5086951725181633875" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1100493834?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina  Kondrenko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina  Kondrenko" href="/user/show/36306002-katerina-kondrenko">Katerina  Kondrenko</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=imo-better-than-i-thought">imo-better-than-i-thought</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=characters-book-boyfriends">characters-book-boyfriends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=trope-magic">trope-magic</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=plot-driven-by-everything">plot-driven-by-everything</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=pov-1st-person">pov-1st-person</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1100493834" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2447581634615297620"><b>
  <blockquote>7 out of 10</blockquote>
</b><br/><b>Ревью в моем блоге/This review on my blog <a href='http://living-a-thousand-lives.blogspot.ru/2016/01/the-girl-of-fire-and-thorns-by-rae.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Living A Thousand Lives</a></b> <i>(please use Chrome/Yandex browser or Android/IOS to see the page; otherwise, spoiler-tags I use to make my post compact may not work)</i><br/><br/><b>Short-Soundtrack:</b><br/><a href='http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=05MKdXeglS0' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fyre – Away From Home</a><br/><a href='http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4E4-9yKTv_I' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Katie Melua – The Flood</a><br/><a href='http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=hRs0PImOizQ' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Les Friction – Firewall</a><br/><br/><b>Genre</b>: high-fantasy, YA<br/><b>Stuff</b>: ugly duckling, Spanish tune, court intrigues, dessert<br/><b>Fail</b>: too much religion and fat-talks<br/><b>WOW</b>: MC's transformation <br/><b>POV</b>: 1st-person, female<br/><b>Love-Geometry</b>: seeming, almost zer</span>
  <span id="freeText2447581634615297620" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>7 out of 10</blockquote>
</b><br /><b>Ревью в моем блоге/This review on my blog <a href="http://living-a-thousand-lives.blogspot.ru/2016/01/the-girl-of-fire-and-thorns-by-rae.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Living A Thousand Lives</a></b> <i>(please use Chrome/Yandex browser or Android/IOS to see the page; otherwise, spoiler-tags I use to make my post compact may not work)</i><br /><br /><b>Short-Soundtrack:</b><br /><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=05MKdXeglS0" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Fyre – Away From Home</a><br /><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4E4-9yKTv_I" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Katie Melua – The Flood</a><br /><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=hRs0PImOizQ" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Les Friction – Firewall</a><br /><br /><b>Genre</b>: high-fantasy, YA<br /><b>Stuff</b>: ugly duckling, Spanish tune, court intrigues, dessert<br /><b>Fail</b>: too much religion and fat-talks<br /><b>WOW</b>: MC's transformation <br /><b>POV</b>: 1st-person, female<br /><b>Love-Geometry</b>: seeming, almost zero<br /><br /><b>Quote-Core</b>: <blockquote>
  <i>
    “I loved and lost and survived.”
  </i>
</blockquote><br />I wasn't planning to read this soon and then my dear friend <b>Nastassja</b> decided to know whether the hype about <i>The Girl of Fire and Thorns</i> (I almost wrote of 'Thorns and Roses', ahaha) is just. After that, she said, 'You go and read, you GO and READ, but beware, the real fan will start in the second book only'. Here I am, Nastya. Here I am.<br /><br /><b>What does your typical YA-heroine look like? I think she’s pretty and gorgeous, though has no idea about it. Meet Elisa, she’s clumsy, average, fat and she’s very aware of it.</b><br /><br />Our MC is only 16 and she becomes a wife of a mature widower (~30 year-old, I guess) with a young child, a kingdom (yup, he's king) to protect (a war is looming on horizon) and a beautiful mistress with questionable intentions and awful personality. She falls for her husband, but understands that he wouldn't love her back, not the way she wants him to. What hurts even more is that, after returning to Alejandro's homeland, the king prefers to keep their marriage in secret. As well as Elisa's specialty: she has a jewel in her navel (disgusting), this stone answers to her devotions and is able to worry her about dangers. This thing is a sign of God's choice, of Elisa's sacred status and her potential heroism. But again, she's a young fat girl (I repeat it only because this fact was repeating on every freaking page of the book, I swear), who would rather eat another pastry instead of saving the world. That's how our story begins.<br /><br />To be honest, <b>I didn't like Elisa at the start</b>, I was getting the point of every character in this story, even of a stupid mistress of Alejandro, but not MCs. She was eating, eating, eating and complaining about her sausage-like appearance. What encouraged me to go on? I knew she would change, I knew she'd become a badass queen, so I was eager to see HOW. And I was eager for her to charm Alejandro (this desire was fading away though, 'since the king was an uncertain person with great responsibilities and inability to fulfill his duties (it's not about sex, ahahah, just saying) to the country (told ya)). I mean, Alejandro wasn't the person I can respect, he had his strengths and pluses, and I was under his spell, but something in him was off, that's why I wasn't obsess with Elisa and him being together no matter what.<br /><br />Wanna know what happened next? What pushed MC? It was a <b>kidnapping</b>. Elisa had traveled through dessert enduring hunger and thirst, was leading a group of rebels and that's only a top of this iceberg. She met a true love in the journey, true friends, true self and became stronger. That's how I start to see Elisa in different lights. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>Little notes:</i>
</b><br />- The pacing was very fast, I spent a night without sleep for the sake of this story and I regret nothing.<br />- I did love Spanish details, Carsons's world reminds me about Spanish south, where Moresco influence was the strongest of all the country. I was reading this book in Russian, but I guess that the classic language was Castellano. Since I love Spain and its language muuuch, I was really pleased with such details. <br />- Religion stuff were irritating, but not overwhelming. <br />- Romantic line had a seeming love-triangle, though there was none, to be honest. And all the romance stuff was very unusual for YA. <br />- MC wasn't the most desired girl in the world, nor the smartest one. <br /> <br /><b>The final</b> includes a few unexpected twists. If I didn't know better, I may end up being really confused. I heard that the second book is a ten million times better (Nastassja, hello!), so I'm pretty curious about the sequel.<br /><br /><b>Fire and Thorns (Шипы и огонь):</b><br /><blockquote>— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1100502479" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shadow Cats (Призрачные кошки)</a> #0.5/3<br />— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1100502494" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shattered Mountain (Треснувшая гора)</a> #0.6/3<br />— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1100501096" rel="nofollow noopener">The King's Guard (Королевский гвардеец)</a> #0.7/3<br />— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1100493834" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl of Fire and Thorns (Книга шипов и огня)</a> #1/3<br />— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1100498766" rel="nofollow noopener">The Crown of Embers (Корона из пепла)</a> #2/3<br />— The Bitter Kingdom (Жестокое царство) #3/3 </blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="2447581634615297620" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5549757545897083180">DNF at 9%. I really wanted to like this book. It's just sad is I begun reading there was just something missing. I don't know what it was. I just didn't really care that much about what happened. And I know I did not read very far but I just didn't care too. It's not a terrible book persay. I definitely wante</span>
  <span id="freeText5549757545897083180" style="display:none">DNF at 9%. I really wanted to like this book. It's just sad is I begun reading there was just something missing. I don't know what it was. I just didn't really care that much about what happened. And I know I did not read very far but I just didn't care too. It's not a terrible book persay. From where I got to it she's not particularly interesting. And maybe I can't judge because I didn't get part all but I just didn't care. It wasn't like I hated it or anything. I don't know. I definitely wanted to like it though. I just don't really see the point in reading it further if it's not interesting to me though. Though maybe if you read it you might like it.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_463450900" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/463450900" />
    <a title="Summer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14778159-summer"><img alt="Summer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574406694p2/14778159.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/463450900?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Summer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Summer" href="/user/show/14778159-summer">Summer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those with very low standards for YA fantasy</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14778159-summer?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer463450900" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10877219126704589131">I have put off this review long enough. It should be telling enough that to this day I preserve a place in my heart that severely abhors this book; it has left that much of an impact on <s>my anger</s> me.<br/><br/>The reason I read this? I wanted to read a high fantasy book that would be reminiscent of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17926775.Stolen_Songbird__The_Malediction_Trilogy___1_' title='Stolen Songbird (The Malediction Trilogy, #1) by Danielle L. Jensen' rel='nofollow noopener'>Stolen Songbird</a>, a recent favorite of mine, and wanted to relive the experience but in a different book. Actually--screw it--imma go right out and say that the <b>sole</b> reason I read <i>The Girl of Fire and Thorns</i> was b</span>
  <span id="freeText10877219126704589131" style="display:none">I have put off this review long enough. It should be telling enough that to this day I preserve a place in my heart that severely abhors this book; it has left that much of an impact on <s>my anger</s> me.<br><br>The reason I read this? I wanted to read a high fantasy book that would be reminiscent of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17926775.Stolen_Songbird__The_Malediction_Trilogy___1_" title="Stolen Songbird (The Malediction Trilogy, #1) by Danielle L. Jensen" rel="nofollow noopener">Stolen Songbird</a>, a recent favorite of mine, and wanted to relive the experience but in a different book. Actually--screw it--imma go right out and say that the <b>sole</b> reason I read <i>The Girl of Fire and Thorns</i> was because I had bought the second book last year for like $1.99 and I wanted to get this series out of the way. <br><br>I didn't expect to love this. But neither did I expect to hate it to this extent.<br><br>The first chapter was decent enough. The storyline in itself is not a bad one, but after Elisa leaves the palace, shit goes awry. I hadn't minded the story until then, but once there’s a lot less courtly-stuff and a lot more magical WTFery, I <i>definitely</i> began to mind.<br><br>I’ll start with the aforementioned magical WTFery. You know in good fantasy books, like <i>Harry Potter</i>, where the magic does not make a bit of rational sense, <s>I AM LYING HEHEHE MUGGLES</s> but you still understand, because it’s fiction, right? You still understand the fundamentals of the magic, you understand that there are these spells, and they work like this, and whatever? Yeah--no, this book doesn't have that. It’s just some random ass magic from a magic ass stone stuck in Elisa’s belly button that just <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[MAGICALLY (pun intended duh) helps her at the most opportune moments. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> At these points, I could literally see the author’s hand making adjustments like a chessboard to further the plot (okay, not literally).<br><br>Not only did the magic make absolutely no sense--or as much sense as magic could make--the fantasy was terrible. It was as generic as those nasty rip-off Oreos at the grocery store. I should start a new genre called Fake Fantasy, and this would be the first book labeled as thus. You know what? <i>The Girl of Fire and Thorns</i> is to the fantasy genre as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11410430.Defiance__Defiance__1_" title="Defiance (Defiance #1) by C.J. Redwine" rel="nofollow noopener">Defiance</a> is to dystopia, and if you've read that book (and disliked it) you’d know what I mean. <br><br>Then there’s Elisa, my favorite character in all of YA fantasy (heh). Oh, God, she was intolerable. She was not that bad at the beginning of the book, and I feel like some teens would be able to relate to her and even like her on some level. But once I passed that line between palace and desert, she became unbearably annoying and whiny and… skinny! Yes, <b>the girl that I was excited to read about, probably one of the only “fat” girls in YA fantasy, magically turned skinny after a month’s treck in the desert.</b> And somehow all her problems just <i>magically</i> evaporated. Man, I wish I could spend a month in the desert and come back home to all my problems being solved. Wait, <i>life doesn't work like that.</i> <br><br>Learn from this, girls: the only way you can get what you want is by losing weight. Lose those love handles, throw away that bag of chips, or else you sure as hell won’t be achieving anything in your life. *sigh*<br><br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-Baujyx4vGpY/VMCG1b3ggzI/AAAAAAAABe0/N60jj6n0Ghg/s1600/animated-rampage.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1421903627ra/13427961.gif" height="239" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><br>(Sidenote: I’m genuinely curious what the author was trying to do with this? How could someone not be offended by this? Not that I think that fiction should be censored, but truly, there had to have been a reason behind this blatant issue that I’m missing.)<br><br>The rest of the characters? Nothing too significant about any of them. I mean, screw characterization, right? In all seriousness, though, the characters were very minimally developed. <u>I began to categorize characters based on whether or not they liked Elisa, because that’s as deep a description as they got.</u> If you like character-based novels, or even if you expect more characterization than the superficial, then you’re in for a big disappointment. <br><br>The romance was, in one very long word (?): blehhhhhhhh. That’s all I’m going to say as I’ll probably spoil approximately the entire book if I let myself go on this diatribe.<br><br>The plot: just kept going on. And on. And on. To nowhere. Absolutely nothing happened along the way. This was one long-ass book, and for a book this long, I’d expect more than never-ending walks. Heck, I’m pretty sure the plot was lost along the way of one of Elisa’s never-ending treads. Where’d ya go, plot?<br><br>While I’m at it, I’ll tick off the other boxes: Worldbuilding? Nonexistent. Writing? Mediocre. Pacing? LOL.<br><br>The only people I’d recommend this to are for those with very, <i>very</i> low standards for young adult fantasy, and even then, I’d warn them of the oncoming disaster.<br><br>#rantover<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="10877219126704589131" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

		    <b>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fej8JGNF9BC7QbA8poKrGVUxx1TJ2Ml3r/ftIGjA5pnw7GkT5yULO6tQXP4SOq6IUGt/z93nYhywQIdWdR2RLQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mdlfmgZKBMCDFhq9G3/K8MChmp6IrgJlnj2uB3VgCxoU3cqtgir765MH9n+vx89hxfsiBZyRqQ6BisRxaL18rg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16275794502946740928">Rae Carson was born in 1973 in California and now lives in Arizona. She developed an enthusiasm for storytelling in her earliest childhood. She studied social sciences and worked in various industries after graduating from university before she realized her dream and became a writer. The Girl of Fire and Thorns is her debut novel.<br/><br/>In her own words, she "write[s] books about teens who must do brave </span>
  <span id="freeText16275794502946740928" style="display:none">Rae Carson was born in 1973 in California and now lives in Arizona. She developed an enthusiasm for storytelling in her earliest childhood. She studied social sciences and worked in various industries after graduating from university before she realized her dream and became a writer. The Girl of Fire and Thorns is her debut novel.<br /><br />In her own words, she "write[s] books about teens who must do brave things. [Her] books tend to contain lots of adventure, a little magic and romance, and smart girls who make (mostly) smart choices. [She] especially love[s] to write about questions [she doesn't] know the answers to."</span>
